<p><b>Dortmund</b> (<span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[ˈdɔɐ̯tmʊnt]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:De-Dortmund.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0e/De-Dortmund.ogg" class="internal" title="De-Dortmund.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>; <a href="/wiki/Low_German_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Low German language">Low German</a>: <span lang="nds"><i>Düörpm</i></span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[ˈdyːœɐ̯pm̩]</span>; <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <span lang="la"><i>Tremonia</i></span>) is an <a href="/wiki/Independent_city" title="Independent city">independent city</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="North Rhine-Westphalia">North Rhine-Westphalia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>. It is in the middle part of the state and is considered to be the administrative, commercial and cultural centre of the eastern <a href="/wiki/Ruhr_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruhr area">Ruhr area</a>. Its population of 581,612 (2015) makes it the 8th largest city in Germany. Moreover, Dortmund is the largest city by area and population in the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruhr Area">Ruhr Area</a>, an urban area with some 5.1 million (2011) inhabitants which is the largest urban agglomeration in Germany.</p>
<p>Founded around 882,<sup id="cite_ref-WM-document-882_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WM-document-882-2">[2]</a></sup> Dortmund became an <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Free_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Free City">Imperial Free City</a>. Throughout the 13th to 14th centuries, it was the "chief city" of the Rhine, Westphalia, the Netherlands Circle of the <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">Hanseatic League</a>. After the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a> the city was destroyed and decreased in significance until the onset of industrialization. The city then became one of Germany's most important coal, steel and beer centres. Dortmund consequently was one of the most heavily bombed cities in Germany during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. The devastating bombing raids of the 12th March 1945 destroyed 98% of buildings in the inner city center. This bombing raids with more than 1,110 aircraft was a record to a single target in World war II.<sup id="cite_ref-backtonormandy.org_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-backtonormandy.org-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>The region has adapted since the collapse of its century long steel and coal industries and shifted to high technology <a href="/wiki/Biomedical_technology" title="Biomedical technology">biomedical technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Micro_systems_technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Micro systems technology">micro systems technology</a> and also <a href="/wiki/Service_(economics)" title="Service (economics)">services</a>. In 2009, Dortmund was classified as a <i>Node city</i> in the Innovation Cities Index published by 2thinknow<sup id="cite_ref-innovation-cities.com_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-innovation-cities.com-4">[4]</a></sup> and is the most sustainable city in <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-https:.2F.2Fwww.nachhaltigkeitspreis.de.2Fsonstige.2Fenglish-summary.2F_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-https:.2F.2Fwww.nachhaltigkeitspreis.de.2Fsonstige.2Fenglish-summary.2F-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>Dortmund is home to many <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Germany" title="Culture of Germany">cultural</a> and <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Germany" title="Education in Germany">educational</a> institutions, including the <a href="/wiki/Technical_University_of_Dortmund" title="Technical University of Dortmund">Technical University of Dortmund</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dortmund_University_of_Applied_Sciences_and_Arts" title="Dortmund University of Applied Sciences and Arts">Dortmund University of Applied Sciences and Arts</a>, International School of Management and other educational, cultural and administrative facilities with over 49,000 students, many museums, such as <a href="/wiki/Museum_Ostwall" title="Museum Ostwall">Museum Ostwall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Museum_f%C3%BCr_Kunst_und_Kulturgeschichte" title="Museum für Kunst und Kulturgeschichte">Museum of Art and Cultural History</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_Football_Museum" title="German Football Museum">German Football Museum</a>, as well as theatres and music venues like the <a href="/wiki/Theater_Dortmund" title="Theater Dortmund">Koncerthaus</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Opernhaus_Dortmund" title="Opernhaus Dortmund">Opera House of Dortmund</a>. The city is known as Westphalia's "<a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">green</a> metropolis". Nearly half the municipal territory consists of waterways, woodland, agriculture and green spaces with spacious parks such as Westfalenpark and <a href="/wiki/Rombergpark" class="mw-redirect" title="Rombergpark">Rombergpark</a>. This stands in a stark contrast with nearly a hundred years of extensive coal mining and steel milling within the city limits.</p>
<p>Dortmund is home to Ballspielverein Borussia 09 e.V. Dortmund, commonly known as <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a>, a successful club in German <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Dortmund" title="Timeline of Dortmund">Timeline of Dortmund</a></div>
<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:Dortmund-Kupferstich-Merian.png" class="image" title="Kupferstich Matthäus Merians der Stadt Dortmund von 1647"><img alt="Kupferstich Matthäus Merians der Stadt Dortmund von 1647" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Dortmund-Kupferstich-Merian.png/600px-Dortmund-Kupferstich-Merian.png" width="600" height="183" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Dortmund-Kupferstich-Merian.png/900px-Dortmund-Kupferstich-Merian.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Dortmund-Kupferstich-Merian.png/1200px-Dortmund-Kupferstich-Merian.png 2x" data-file-width="2544" data-file-height="776" /></a></div>
<p>The first time Dortmund was mentioned in official documents was around 882.<sup id="cite_ref-WM-document-882_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WM-document-882-2">[2]</a></sup> as <b>Throtmanni</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>After it was destroyed by a fire, the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I_(Barbarossa)" class="mw-redirect" title="Frederick I (Barbarossa)">Frederick I (Barbarossa)</a> had the town rebuilt in 1152 and resided there (among other places) for two years. It became an <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Free_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Free City">Imperial Free City</a>. Throughout the 13th to 14th centuries, it was the "chief city" of the Rhine, Westphalia, the Netherlands Circle of the <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">Hanseatic League</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dortmund_um_1804.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Dortmund_um_1804.jpg/220px-Dortmund_um_1804.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Dortmund_um_1804.jpg/330px-Dortmund_um_1804.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Dortmund_um_1804.jpg/440px-Dortmund_um_1804.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="682" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dortmund_um_1804.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pre-industrial Dortmund 1804</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stadt_Dortmund_1922.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Stadt_Dortmund_1922.jpg/220px-Stadt_Dortmund_1922.jpg" width="220" height="343" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Stadt_Dortmund_1922.jpg/330px-Stadt_Dortmund_1922.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Stadt_Dortmund_1922.jpg/440px-Stadt_Dortmund_1922.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5234" data-file-height="8164" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stadt_Dortmund_1922.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bond of the City of Dortmund, issued 21. June 1922</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After 1320, the city appeared in writing as "Dorpmunde". In the years leading up to 1344, the English King even borrowed money from well-heeled Dortmund merchant families Berswordt and Klepping, offering the regal crown as security. In 1388, Count von Mark joined forces with the Archbishop of <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> and issued declarations of a feud against the town. Following a major siege lasting 18 months, peace negotiations took place and Dortmund emerged victorious. After Cologne was excluded after the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Hanseatic_War" title="Anglo-Hanseatic War">Anglo-Hanseatic War</a> (1470–74), Dortmund was made capital of the Rhine-Westphalian and Netherlands Circle. The <a href="/wiki/List_of_earthquakes_in_Germany" title="List of earthquakes in Germany">1661 earthquake</a> made the <a href="/wiki/Reinoldikirche" class="mw-redirect" title="Reinoldikirche">Reinoldikirche</a> collapse. It was part of <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Berg" title="Grand Duchy of Berg">Grand Duchy of Berg</a> between 1806 and 1813 before passing to Prussian rule. The state mining authority of the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruhr area">Ruhr area</a> was founded in 1815 and moved from Bochum to Dortmund. Within the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Prussian</a> <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Westphalia" title="Province of Westphalia">Province of Westphalia</a>, Dortmund was a district seat within <a href="/wiki/Regierungsbezirk_Arnsberg" class="mw-redirect" title="Regierungsbezirk Arnsberg">Regierungsbezirk Arnsberg</a> until 1875, when it became an urban district within the region.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alte_Markt_Dortmund.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Alte_Markt_Dortmund.JPG/220px-Alte_Markt_Dortmund.JPG" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Alte_Markt_Dortmund.JPG/330px-Alte_Markt_Dortmund.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Alte_Markt_Dortmund.JPG/440px-Alte_Markt_Dortmund.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2112" data-file-height="2816" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alte_Markt_Dortmund.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Old market <a href="/wiki/St._Reinoldi_(Dortmund)" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Reinoldi (Dortmund)">St. Reinolds</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Industrialisation" title="Industrialisation">industrialisation</a> of Prussia, Dortmund became a major centre for <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steel" title="Steel">steel</a>. The town expanded into a city, with the population rising from 57,742 in 1875 to 379,950 in 1905. Sprawling residential areas like the North, East, Union and Kreuz district sprang up in less than 10 years. In 1920, Dortmund was one of the centres for resistance to the <a href="/wiki/Kapp_Putsch" title="Kapp Putsch">Kapp Putsch</a> - a right military coup launched against the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic" class="mw-redirect" title="Social Democratic">Social Democratic</a>-led government. Radical workers formed a <a href="/wiki/Ruhr_Red_Army" title="Ruhr Red Army">Red Army</a> who fought the <a href="/wiki/Freikorps" title="Freikorps">freikorps</a> units involved in the coup.</p>
<p>Under <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Old_Synagogue_(Dortmund)" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Synagogue (Dortmund)">Old synagogue</a> was destroyed in 1938. Also, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aplerbeck_Hospital&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Aplerbeck Hospital (page does not exist)">Aplerbeck Hospital</a> in Dortmund transferred mentally and/or physically disabled patients for euthanasia at the <a href="/wiki/Hadamar_Clinic" class="mw-redirect" title="Hadamar Clinic">Hadamar mental hospital</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Action_T4" class="mw-redirect" title="Action T4">Action T4</a> (an additional 229 children were killed in the "Children's Specialist Department", which was transferred from Marburg in 1941). Bombing targets of the <a href="/wiki/Oil_Campaign_of_World_War_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil Campaign of World War II">Oil Campaign of World War II</a> in Dortmund included <a href="/wiki/Westfalenh%C3%BCtte" title="Westfalenhütte">Hoesch-Westfalenhütte AG</a>, the "<a href="/wiki/Hoesch_AG" title="Hoesch AG">Hoesch</a>-Benzin GmbH" synthetic oil plant, and the <i>Zeche Hansa</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The bombings destroyed about 66% of Dortmund homes.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The devastating bombing raids of the 12th March 1945 with 1,108 aircraft (748 Lancasters, 292 Halifaxes, 68 Mosquitos) destroyed 98% of buildings in the inner city center and 4,851 tonnes of bombs were dropped through Dortmund city centre and the south of the city; this was a record to a single target in the whole of World war II.<sup id="cite_ref-backtonormandy.org_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-backtonormandy.org-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Code_word" title="Code word">code word</a> <i>Dortmund</i> was radioed to initiate the 1941 <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa" title="Operation Barbarossa">Operation Barbarossa</a> campaign against the Soviet Union. The Allied ground advance into Germany reached Dortmund in April 1945. The US <a href="/wiki/95th_Infantry_Division_(United_States)" title="95th Infantry Division (United States)">95th Infantry Division</a>, attacked the city on 12 April 1945 against a spirited German defense. The division, assisted by close air support, advanced through the ruins in urban combat and completed its capture on 13 April 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the war, buildings such as the main churches <a href="/wiki/Reinoldikirche" class="mw-redirect" title="Reinoldikirche">Reinoldikirche</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marienkirche,_Dortmund" title="Marienkirche, Dortmund">Marienkirche</a> were restored or rebuilt, and extensive parks and gardens were laid out. The simple but successful postwar rebuilding has resulted in a very mixed and unique cityscape. The <a href="/wiki/Zollern_II/IV_Colliery" title="Zollern II/IV Colliery">LWL-Industriemuseum</a> was founded in 1969,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> and the city subsequently became a regional centre for hi-tech industry.</p>
<p>On 3 November 2013, more than 20,000 people were evacuated after a <a href="/wiki/Blockbuster_bomb" title="Blockbuster bomb">4,000-pound bomb</a> from <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> was found. German authorities safely defused the bomb. The bomb was found after analysing old <a href="/wiki/Aerial_photography" title="Aerial photography">aerial photographs</a> while searching for unexploded bombs dropped by <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied</a> aircraft over Germany's industrial <a href="/wiki/Ruhr" title="Ruhr">Ruhr</a> region.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Location">Location</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Location">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dortmund is an independent city located in the east of the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr" title="Ruhr">Ruhr</a> area, one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban areas</a> in Europe (see also: <a href="/wiki/Megalopolis_(city_type)" class="mw-redirect" title="Megalopolis (city type)">megalopolis</a>), comprising eleven <a href="/wiki/Independent_city" title="Independent city">independent cities</a> and four <a href="/wiki/District" title="District">districts</a> with some 5.3 million inhabitants. The city limits of Dortmund itself are 87&#160;km (54&#160;mi) long and border twelve cities, two independent and ten <i>kreisangehörig</i> (i.e., belonging to a district), with a total population of approximately 2.4 million. The following cities border Dortmund (clockwise starting from north-east): <a href="/wiki/Bochum" title="Bochum">Bochum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Castrop-Rauxel" title="Castrop-Rauxel">Castrop-Rauxel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waltrop" title="Waltrop">Waltrop</a>, <a href="/wiki/L%C3%BCnen" title="Lünen">Lünen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kamen" title="Kamen">Kamen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unna" title="Unna">Unna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holzwickede" title="Holzwickede">Holzwickede</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schwerte" title="Schwerte">Schwerte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hagen" title="Hagen">Hagen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herdecke" title="Herdecke">Herdecke</a> and <a href="/wiki/Witten" title="Witten">Witten</a>. Historically speaking, Dortmund is a part of <a href="/wiki/Westphalia" title="Westphalia">Westphalia</a> which is situated in the Bundesland North Rhine-Westphalia. Moreover, Dortmund is part of <a href="/wiki/Westphalian_Lowland" title="Westphalian Lowland">Westphalian Lowland</a> and adjoins with the <a href="/wiki/Ardey_Hills" title="Ardey Hills">Ardey Hills</a> in the south of the city to the <a href="/wiki/Sauerland" title="Sauerland">Sauerland</a>.</p>
<p>The lowest point can be found in the northern borough of Brechten at 48,9m, the highest point in the borough of Syburg at 254,3 m.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boroughs">Boroughs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Boroughs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dortmund_Bezirke_und_Nachbargemeinden.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Dortmund_Bezirke_und_Nachbargemeinden.png/220px-Dortmund_Bezirke_und_Nachbargemeinden.png" width="220" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Dortmund_Bezirke_und_Nachbargemeinden.png/330px-Dortmund_Bezirke_und_Nachbargemeinden.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Dortmund_Bezirke_und_Nachbargemeinden.png/440px-Dortmund_Bezirke_und_Nachbargemeinden.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1021" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dortmund_Bezirke_und_Nachbargemeinden.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Municipalities and neighbouring communities</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Dortmund comprises 62 neighbourhoods which in turn are grouped into twelve boroughs (called <i>Stadtbezirke</i>), often named after the most important neighbourhood. Three boroughs cover the area of the inner city (Innenstadt-West, Innenstadt-Nord, Innenstadt-Ost) and the remaining nine boroughs make up the surrounding area (<a href="/wiki/Eving" title="Eving">Eving</a>, Scharnhorst, Brackel, Aplerbeck, <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B6rde" title="Hörde">Hörde</a>, Hombruch, Lütgendortmund, Huckarde, Mengede). Each <i>Stadtbezirk</i> is assigned a Roman numeral and has a local governing body of nineteen members with limited authority. Most of the boroughs were originally independent municipalities but were gradually annexed from 1905 to 1975. This long-lasting process of annexation has led to a strong identification of the population with "their" boroughs or districts and to a rare peculiarity: The borough of Hörde, located in the south of Dortmund and independent until 1928, has its own coat of arms.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dortmund is situated in the <a href="/wiki/Temperateness" class="mw-redirect" title="Temperateness">temperate climate zone</a>. Winters are comparatively mild, summers rather cool. The average annual temperature lies at approximately 9 to 10&#160;°C (48 to 50&#160;°F), the total average annual amount of precipitation lies at approximately 800&#160;mm (31&#160;in). Precipitation evenly falls throughout the year; steady rain (with some snow), prevails in the wintertime, isolated showers dominate the summer season. Dortmund features characteristics of densely populated areas as for example the occurrence of <a href="/wiki/Urban_heat_islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban heat islands">urban heat islands</a> is typical.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dortmund_population.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Dortmund_population.svg/250px-Dortmund_population.svg.png" width="250" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Dortmund_population.svg/375px-Dortmund_population.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Dortmund_population.svg/500px-Dortmund_population.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="400" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dortmund_population.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Population Development since 1400</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Dortmund's population grew rapidly in the time of the 19th century industrialisation when coal mining and steel processing in the city began. 1904 marks the year when Dortmund saw a population of more than 100,000 for the first time in its history. During the 19th century the area around Dortmund called <a href="/wiki/Ruhr" title="Ruhr">Ruhr</a> attracted up to 500,000 ethnic <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mazurs" class="mw-redirect" title="Mazurs">Masurians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Silesians" title="Silesians">Silesians</a> from <a href="/wiki/East_Prussia" title="East Prussia">East Prussia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">Silesia</a> in a migration known as <i><a href="/wiki/Ostflucht" title="Ostflucht">Ostflucht</a></i> (flight from the east). Most of the new inhabitants came from Eastern Europe, but immigrants also came from <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>. Almost all their descendants today speak German as a mother tongue, and for various reasons they do not identify with their Polish roots and traditions, often only their Polish family names remaining as a sign of their past. Not taking the fluctuation of war years into account, the population figures rose constantly to 657,804 in 1965. As a result of the city's post-industrial decline, the population fell to just under 580,000 in 2011. Today with a population of 595,624 (2015) the City of Dortmund is <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Germany_by_population" title="List of cities in Germany by population">the eighth largest city in Germany</a> after <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart" title="Stuttgart">Stuttgart</a> and <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf</a>. It is also the largest city in the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr" title="Ruhr">Ruhr</a> agglomeration.</p>
<p>Contrary to earlier projections, population figures have been on the rise in recent years due to net migration gains. Dortmund has seen a moderate influx of younger people (18 to 25 years of age) mainly because of its universities.<sup id="cite_ref-dortmund.de_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dortmund.de-16">[16]</a></sup> Data of the <a href="/wiki/2011_EU_census" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 EU census">EU-wide 2011 census</a> revealed massive inaccuracies with regard to German population figures. Consequently, respective figures have been corrected, which resulted in a statistical "loss" of 9,000 inhabitants in Dortmund.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> In 2016 it was announced that the population was back above 600,000.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Dortmund had a population of 571,403 of whom about 177,000 (roughly 30%) were of non-German origin.<sup id="cite_ref-dortmund.de_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dortmund.de-16">[16]</a></sup> The table shows the number of first and second generation immigrants in Dortmund by nationality as of 31 December 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-dev.statistik.dortmund.de_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dev.statistik.dortmund.de-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gr._Orthodox_Heilige_Apostel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gr._Orthodox_Heilige_Apostel.jpg/220px-Gr._Orthodox_Heilige_Apostel.jpg" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gr._Orthodox_Heilige_Apostel.jpg/330px-Gr._Orthodox_Heilige_Apostel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gr._Orthodox_Heilige_Apostel.jpg/440px-Gr._Orthodox_Heilige_Apostel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="676" data-file-height="676" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gr._Orthodox_Heilige_Apostel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Church of the Holy Apostles</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Dortmund was historically a <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a>-dominated city. However, during the 19th century an increasing number of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Germany">Catholics</a> moved there from <a href="/wiki/East_Prussia" title="East Prussia">East Prussia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">Silesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>. As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the largest Christian denominations were Protestantism (29.9%) and Roman Catholicism (27.4% of the population).<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Furthermore, in Dortmund the Greek Orthodox Church, the Serbian Orthodox Church and the Macedonian Orthodox Church are represented. The Church of the Holy Apostles (gre. I.N. Αγίων Αποστόλων Ντόρτμουντ - I.N. Agíon Apostólon Dortmund) was the first Greek church in Germany to be founded due to the influx of "guest workers". Also Dortmund is home of the New Apostolic Church in <a href="/wiki/North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="North Rhine-Westphalia">North Rhine-Westphalia</a> with more than 84,944 community members.</p>
<p>The Jewish community has a history dating back to Medieval times and has always ranked among the largest in <a href="/wiki/Westphalia" title="Westphalia">Westphalia</a>. Dortmund is home to the National Association of Jewish Communities of Westfalen-Lippe. The synagogues operate there in City center, Hörde and Dorstfeld. Due to the growing immigration of people from Muslim countries beginning in the 1960s. Dortmund has a large Muslim community with more than 30 Mosques.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Dortmund's current Bürgermeister (mayor) is <a href="/wiki/Ullrich_Sierau" title="Ullrich Sierau">Ullrich Sierau</a> with variable majorities between <a href="/wiki/SPD" class="mw-redirect" title="SPD">SPD</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_Union_of_Germany" title="Christian Democratic Union of Germany">CDU</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alliance_%2790/The_Greens" class="mw-redirect" title="Alliance '90/The Greens">Alliance '90/The Greens</a></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_government_past_and_present">City government past and present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: City government past and present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stadtwappen_Dortmund.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Stadtwappen_Dortmund.png/170px-Stadtwappen_Dortmund.png" width="170" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Stadtwappen_Dortmund.png/255px-Stadtwappen_Dortmund.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Stadtwappen_Dortmund.png/340px-Stadtwappen_Dortmund.png 2x" data-file-width="550" data-file-height="556" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stadtwappen_Dortmund.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dortmund coat of arms</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Friedensplatz_Rathaus_Dortmund.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Friedensplatz_Rathaus_Dortmund.jpg/220px-Friedensplatz_Rathaus_Dortmund.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Friedensplatz_Rathaus_Dortmund.jpg/330px-Friedensplatz_Rathaus_Dortmund.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Friedensplatz_Rathaus_Dortmund.jpg/440px-Friedensplatz_Rathaus_Dortmund.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Friedensplatz_Rathaus_Dortmund.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dortmund town hall</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Dortmund is one of nineteen <a href="/wiki/Independent_city" title="Independent city">independent district-free cities</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Urban_districts_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban districts of Germany">kreisfreie Städte</a></i>) in <a href="/wiki/North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="North Rhine-Westphalia">North Rhine-Westphalia</a>, which means that it does not form part of another general-purpose local government entity, in this case it is not part of a <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_rural_districts_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="List of rural districts of Germany">Landkreis</a>'</i></p>
<p>Dortmund is often called the <i>Herzkammer der SPD</i> (roughly translated as "heartland of the Social democrats"), which is the politically dominant party in the city. During the Nazi era (1933–1945), mayors were installed by the Nazi Party. After World War II, the military government of the British occupation zone installed a new mayor and a municipal constitution modeled on that of British cities. The first major elected by the population of Dortmund was <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Hen%C3%9Fler" title="Fritz Henßler">Fritz Henßler</a>. Since the end of the war, the SPD has held a relative majority in the town council - except from 1999 to 2004. Since the 2012 local election, there have been 8 parties and electors' groups in the town council (86 seats; 2009: 96 seats): <a href="/wiki/Ullrich_Sierau" title="Ullrich Sierau">Ullrich Sierau</a> (SPD) has been the mayor of Dortmund since May 2010. He has had to work with changing majorities in the local council.</p>
<p>The last municipal election was held on 25.&#160;May 2014. The SPD reached 38,2% (36 seats), CDU 27,2% (26 seats), die Grünen 15,4% (15 seats), Die Linke 6,8% (6 seats), the AfD 3,4% (3 seats), the FDP 2,4% (2 seats), Piraten 2,3% (2 seats), Die Rechte 1,0% (1 seat), the Bürgerliste für Dortmund 1,0% (1 seat), the NPD 0,9% (1 seat) und the Freie Bürger-Initiative 0,7% (1 seats).</p>
<p><b>Current composition of the local council (July 2014):</b></p>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dortmund_Panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Dortmund_Panorama.jpg/220px-Dortmund_Panorama.jpg" width="220" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Dortmund_Panorama.jpg/330px-Dortmund_Panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Dortmund_Panorama.jpg/440px-Dortmund_Panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="1892" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dortmund_Panorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dortmund with RWE-Tower and churches of Reinoldi, Petri and Marien on the right</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Dortmund's city centre offers a picture full of contrasts. Historic buildings like <a href="/wiki/Altes_Stadthaus,_Dortmund" title="Altes Stadthaus, Dortmund">Altes Stadthaus</a> or the Krügerpassage rub shoulders with post-war architecture like Gesundheitshaus and concrete constructions with Romanesque churches like the <a href="/wiki/Reinoldikirche" class="mw-redirect" title="Reinoldikirche">Reinoldikirche</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Marienkirche,_Dortmund" title="Marienkirche, Dortmund">Marienkirche</a>. The near-complete destruction of Dortmund's city centre during World War&#160;II (98%) has resulted in a varied architectural landscape. The reconstruction of the city followed the style of the 1950s, while respecting the old layout and naming of the streets. The downtown of Dortmund still retains the outline of the medieval city. A ring road marks the former city wall, and the <a href="/wiki/Hellweg" title="Hellweg">Westen-/Ostenhellweg</a>, part of a medieval salt trading route, is still the major (pedestrian) street bisecting the city centre.</p>
<p>Thus, the city today is characterized by simple and modest post-war buildings, with a few interspersed pre-war buildings which were reconstructed due to their historical importance. Some buildings of the "Wiederaufbauzeit" (era of reconstruction), for example the opera house are nowadays regarded as classics of modern architecture.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_districts">Urban districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Urban districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Unlike the Dortmund city centre, much of the inner districts around the old medieval centre escaped damage in the second world war and post war redevelopment.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kreuzviertel">Kreuzviertel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Kreuzviertel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kreuzstra%C3%9Fe.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Kreuzstra%C3%9Fe.JPG/220px-Kreuzstra%C3%9Fe.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Kreuzstra%C3%9Fe.JPG/330px-Kreuzstra%C3%9Fe.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Kreuzstra%C3%9Fe.JPG/440px-Kreuzstra%C3%9Fe.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kreuzstra%C3%9Fe.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Typical Wilhelminian style houses</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Kreuzviertel is characterised by old buildings, the majority of which come from the turn of the 20th century (1884 to 1908). Over 80% of all housing in this area was constructed before 1948, with the oldest building the Dortmund University of Applied Sciences and Arts still standing being from 1896. In the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">second World War</a>, relatively few buildings were destroyed in comparison to other areas of the city. Today, Kreuzviertel forms a nearly homogeneous historic building area. Over 100 buildings remain protected as historic monuments, like the Kreuzkirche at Kreuzstraße and the first Concrete Church in Germany St.-Nicolai. Nowadays the Kreuzviertel is a trendy district with pubs, restaurants, cafés, galleries and little shops. The west park is the green lung of the Downtown of Dortmund and in the months between May and October a centre of the student urban life.</p>
<p>Even today many artists choose Kreuzviertel as their residence: <a href="/wiki/Sascha_Schmitz" title="Sascha Schmitz">Sascha Schmitz</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Matthias_Nadolny&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Matthias Nadolny (page does not exist)">Matthias Nadolny</a> and players of <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Nordstadt">Nordstadt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Nordstadt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dortmund_Borsigplatz_Kreisverkehr.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Dortmund_Borsigplatz_Kreisverkehr.JPG/220px-Dortmund_Borsigplatz_Kreisverkehr.JPG" width="220" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Dortmund_Borsigplatz_Kreisverkehr.JPG/330px-Dortmund_Borsigplatz_Kreisverkehr.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Dortmund_Borsigplatz_Kreisverkehr.JPG/440px-Dortmund_Borsigplatz_Kreisverkehr.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3033" data-file-height="2449" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dortmund_Borsigplatz_Kreisverkehr.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Borsigplatz, home of the BVB</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The northern part of Dortmund called Nordstadt, situated in a territory of 14.42&#160;km² is shaped by a colorful variety of cultures. As the largest homogeneous old building area in <a href="/wiki/Ruhr" title="Ruhr">Ruhr</a> the Nordstadt is a melting pot of different people of different countries and habits just a few steps from the city center. The Nordstadt is an industrial <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban area</a> that was mainly developed in the 19th Century to serve the <a href="/wiki/Westfalenh%C3%BCtte" title="Westfalenhütte">Westfalenhütte</a> steelworks, port and rail freight depot. All of the residents live in a densely populated 300 hectare area (the most densely populated residential area in the state of <a href="/wiki/North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="North Rhine-Westphalia">North Rhine-Westphalia</a> with steelworks, port and railway lines acting as physical barriers cutting off the area from the city centre and other residential districts).<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>The area has been badly affected by the deindustrialisation of these heavy industries, with the target area developing a role as the home for growing numbers of immigrants and socially disadvantaged groups partly because of the availability of cheaper (although poor quality) accommodation. <sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>Nevertheless, two parks – Fredenbaumpark and Hoeschpark – are situated there. There is also much equipment for children to spend their free time. For example, the 35 meters high Big Tipi, which was brought in from the <a href="/wiki/Expo_2000" title="Expo 2000">Expo 2000</a> in Hanover. All of that should attract families to settle in, but low prices of apartments and a variety of renting offers speak for the contrary. This developed into the youngest population of Dortmund is living and created a district with art house cinemas to ethnic stores, from exotic restaurants to student pubs.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Borsigplatz is probably one of the best known squares in the Nordstadt. Ballspielverein <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a> was founded nearby, north-east of the main railway station. The streets radiating outward to form a star shape, the sycamore in the middle of the square and the tramline running diagonally across the square give Borsigplatz its very own flair. <sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kaiserviertel">Kaiserviertel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Kaiserviertel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dortmund_Kaiserstra%C3%9Fenviertel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Dortmund_Kaiserstra%C3%9Fenviertel.jpg/220px-Dortmund_Kaiserstra%C3%9Fenviertel.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Dortmund_Kaiserstra%C3%9Fenviertel.jpg/330px-Dortmund_Kaiserstra%C3%9Fenviertel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Dortmund_Kaiserstra%C3%9Fenviertel.jpg/440px-Dortmund_Kaiserstra%C3%9Fenviertel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dortmund_Kaiserstra%C3%9Fenviertel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cherry Blossom Avenue</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Kaiserstraßen District is located east of the former ramparts of Dortmund and follows the course of the <a href="/wiki/Westenhellweg" title="Westenhellweg">Westenhellweg</a>. In this district numerous magnificent buildings from the 1900s and new buildings from the 1950s are located next to the heritage-protected State Mining Office Dortmund, several Courts, Consulate and the East Cemetery. The district is characterize by the employee of the Amtsgericht, Landgericht (the first and second instances of ordinary jurisdiction) and the Prison.</p>
<p>Today the historical Kaiserbrunnen and the entrance sign for Kaiserstraße are important starting points for a tour to the popular shopping district. The Moltkestreet also known as the Cherry Blossom Avenue, became famous after photographers started posting pictures of blooming trees. Every spring, usually in April, the street in the Kaiserstraßen district is booming with pink blossoms and attracts tourists.</p>
<h4><span id="Hörde_on_the_Lake_Phoenix"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="H.C3.B6rde_on_the_Lake_Phoenix">Hörde on the Lake Phoenix</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Hörde on the Lake Phoenix">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marktplatz_Hoerde.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Marktplatz_Hoerde.jpg/220px-Marktplatz_Hoerde.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Marktplatz_Hoerde.jpg/330px-Marktplatz_Hoerde.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Marktplatz_Hoerde.jpg/440px-Marktplatz_Hoerde.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marktplatz_Hoerde.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Old town Hörde</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dortmund_-_PO-Phoenix-See_%2B_H%C3%B6rde_01_ies.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Dortmund_-_PO-Phoenix-See_%2B_H%C3%B6rde_01_ies.jpg/220px-Dortmund_-_PO-Phoenix-See_%2B_H%C3%B6rde_01_ies.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Dortmund_-_PO-Phoenix-See_%2B_H%C3%B6rde_01_ies.jpg/330px-Dortmund_-_PO-Phoenix-See_%2B_H%C3%B6rde_01_ies.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Dortmund_-_PO-Phoenix-See_%2B_H%C3%B6rde_01_ies.jpg/440px-Dortmund_-_PO-Phoenix-See_%2B_H%C3%B6rde_01_ies.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dortmund_-_PO-Phoenix-See_%2B_H%C3%B6rde_01_ies.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lake Phoenix</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hörde is borough in the south of the city of Dortmund. Originally Hörde was a separate town (until 1929) and was founded by the Counts of Mark in opposition to their principal enemy, the town of Dortmund. In 1388, the "Großen Dortmunder Fehde" (great feud of Dortmund) took place, where the city of Dortmund battled against the alliance of surrounding towns. The struggle ended in 1390, with defeat for Hörde and its allies of <a href="/wiki/Herdecke" title="Herdecke">Herdecke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Witten" title="Witten">Witten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bochum" title="Bochum">Bochum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Castrop" title="Castrop">Castrop</a>, <a href="/wiki/L%C3%BCnen" title="Lünen">Lünen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unna" title="Unna">Unna</a> und <a href="/wiki/Schwerte" title="Schwerte">Schwerte</a>. Today Hörde is a part of Dortmund with restored old buildings combined with modern architecture. The Hörder Burg (Hörde castle) was built in the 12th century and is located in the east of the town, close to the <a href="/wiki/Emscher" title="Emscher">Emscher</a> and Lake Phoenix.</p>
<p>Lake Phoenix was one of the largest urban redevelopment projects in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>. On the area of the former blast furnace and steel plant site of <a href="/wiki/ThyssenKrupp" title="ThyssenKrupp">ThyssenKrupp</a> newly formed and developed a new urban resident and recreational area 3 kilometers (2.6 miles) from the city centre of Dortmund. The development of the Phoenix See area cost 170 million Euro.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The lake is 1,2&#160;km long directed to east-west and 320 meters wide in north-south direction. The water surface area of 24 acres is larger than the <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a> <a href="/wiki/Alster" title="Alster">Alster</a>. Lake Phoenix is a shallow water lake with a depth of 3 to 4 meters and a capacity of around 600,000 cubic meters. Attractive high priced residential areas were thus created on the southern and northern sides of the Lake. On the western lakeside, the existing district centre of Hörde is enlarged by a city port and a mixed functional urban area.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Phoenixsee_Burgplatz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Phoenixsee_Burgplatz.jpg/220px-Phoenixsee_Burgplatz.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Phoenixsee_Burgplatz.jpg/330px-Phoenixsee_Burgplatz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Phoenixsee_Burgplatz.jpg/440px-Phoenixsee_Burgplatz.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Phoenixsee_Burgplatz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Port promenade and Castle</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Companies with agencies and offices on the lakefront include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zalando" title="Zalando">Zalando</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/HSBC_Trinkaus" title="HSBC Trinkaus">HSBC Trinkaus</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/German_Handball_Association" title="German Handball Association">German Handball Association</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Handball-Bundesliga" title="Handball-Bundesliga">Handball-Bundesliga (HBL)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/German_public_bank" title="German public bank">Academy of the German public Bank</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mircosonic&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mircosonic (page does not exist)">Mircosonic</a></li>
</ul>
<p>The finished sole is primarily fed by groundwater and unpolluted rainwater from the new building sites.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> The River <a href="/wiki/Emscher" title="Emscher">Emscher</a> flows through an embanked riverbed without direct link to the Lake. Together with the renatured Emscher, the Lake forms a water landscape of 33 hectares, which, as a linking area, is an important element of the Emscher landscape park. The renaturation of the Emscher River is managed by the public <a href="/wiki/Water_board" title="Water board">water board</a> <a href="/wiki/Emschergenossenschaft" title="Emschergenossenschaft">Emschergenossenschaft</a>. The financial frame is 4.5 billion Euro and the aim is to finish the main work by the year 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shopping_streets">Shopping streets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Shopping streets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <b>Westenhellweg</b> is a popular shopping destination and with nearly 13,000 visitors per hour it was Germany's most frequented shopping street in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Some of the most reputed shops, department stores, and labels have their stores here. It is a pedestrian-only area and is bordered by the <a href="/wiki/Reinoldikirche" class="mw-redirect" title="Reinoldikirche">Reinoldikirche</a> in the east and <a href="/wiki/Dortmund_U-Tower" title="Dortmund U-Tower">U-Tower</a> in the west. The Westenhellweg has one of the highest rents for retail and office space in <a href="/wiki/North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="North Rhine-Westphalia">North Rhine-Westphalia</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Einkaufsstra%C3%9Fe_Westenhellweg_Dortmund.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Einkaufsstra%C3%9Fe_Westenhellweg_Dortmund.jpg/220px-Einkaufsstra%C3%9Fe_Westenhellweg_Dortmund.jpg" width="220" height="213" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Einkaufsstra%C3%9Fe_Westenhellweg_Dortmund.jpg/330px-Einkaufsstra%C3%9Fe_Westenhellweg_Dortmund.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Einkaufsstra%C3%9Fe_Westenhellweg_Dortmund.jpg/440px-Einkaufsstra%C3%9Fe_Westenhellweg_Dortmund.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2426" data-file-height="2353" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Einkaufsstra%C3%9Fe_Westenhellweg_Dortmund.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Westenhellweg</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>85 percent of the shops are retail chains such as <a href="/wiki/H%26M" title="H&amp;M">H&amp;M</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saturn_(store)" title="Saturn (store)">Saturn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Esprit_Holdings" title="Esprit Holdings">Esprit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zara_(retailer)" title="Zara (retailer)">Zara</a> or <a href="/wiki/NewYorker" title="NewYorker">NewYorker</a>. In 2009 a new shopping mall named <a href="/w/index.php?title=Thier-Galerie&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Thier-Galerie (page does not exist)">Thier-Galerie</a> opened there with nearly 100 stores and chains like <a href="/wiki/Hollister_Co." title="Hollister Co.">Hollister</a>. Three more shopping malls occupy the Thier-Galerie, <a href="/wiki/Metro_AG" title="Metro AG">Galeria Kaufhof</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arcandor" title="Arcandor">Karstadt</a>, as well as large fashion retail clothing stores from <a href="/wiki/Peek_%26_Cloppenburg" title="Peek &amp; Cloppenburg">Peek &amp; Cloppenburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/C%26A" title="C&amp;A">C&amp;A</a>. During the month before <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a>, the extended pedestrian-only zone is host to <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund_Christmas_Market&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dortmund Christmas Market (page does not exist)">Dortmund Christmas Market</a>, one of the largest and oldest Christmas markets in Germany. With more than 3.5 million visitors and 300 stalls around a gigantic Christmas tree that stands 45 metres tall, it is one of the most visited and popular market in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>In close proximity to the Dortmund concert hall lies the <b>Brückstraßenviertel</b> - a quarter hub especially for young people. The "Rue de Pommes Frites", which is what the Dortmund citizens have called the Brückstraße for a long time, has turned into a modern, young shopping promenade.</p>
<p>For a long time the <b>Kampstraße</b> had a shadowy existence as parallel street to the Westenhellweg and Ostenhellweg, but it has now become a grand boulevard which contains specialist stores. Right next to the Kampstraße is the Kleppingstraße, an expensive shopping street with prestigious shops.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Churches">Churches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Churches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marienkirchhof_Dortmund.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Marienkirchhof_Dortmund.jpg/220px-Marienkirchhof_Dortmund.jpg" width="220" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Marienkirchhof_Dortmund.jpg/330px-Marienkirchhof_Dortmund.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Marienkirchhof_Dortmund.jpg/440px-Marienkirchhof_Dortmund.jpg 2x" data-file-width="692" data-file-height="732" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marienkirchhof_Dortmund.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Reinoldikirche and Marienkirche</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Reinoldikirche" class="mw-redirect" title="Reinoldikirche">Reinoldikirche</a>, a Protestant church (built in 1233–1450)</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petrikirche,_Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Petrikirche, Dortmund (page does not exist)">Petrikirche</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petrikirche_(Dortmund)" class="extiw" title="de:Petrikirche (Dortmund)">de</a>)</span>, a now Protestant church (start of construction 1322). It is famous for the huge carved altar (known as "Golden Miracle of Dortmund"), from 1521. It consists of 633 gilt carved oak figures depicting 30 scenes about Easter.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Marienkirche,_Dortmund" title="Marienkirche, Dortmund">Marienkirche</a>, a now Protestant church originally built in 1170–1200 but rebuilt after World War II. The altar is from 1420.</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Propsteikirche,_Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Propsteikirche, Dortmund (page does not exist)">Propsteikirche</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Propsteikirche_St._Johannes_Baptist" class="extiw" title="de:Propsteikirche St. Johannes Baptist">de</a>)</span>, Monastery of the Dominican Order in the city center (built in 1331–1353)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/St._Peter,_Syburg" title="St. Peter, Syburg">St. Peter church</a> in Syburg suburb, the oldest church building in the city limits</li>
<li>Heilig-Kreuz-Kirche, a Protestant church (start of construction 1911)</li>
<li>St.-Margareta Chapel, a Protestant chapel built in 1348</li>
</ul>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional" style="max-width: 978px;_width: 978px;">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Castles">Castles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Castles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Haus Bodelschwingh (13th century), a moated castle</li>
<li>Haus Dellwig (13th century), a moated castle partly rebuilt in the 17th century. The façade and the steep tower, and two half-timbered buildings, are original.</li>
<li>Haus Rodenberg (13th century), a moated castle</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Altes_Stadthaus,_Dortmund" title="Altes Stadthaus, Dortmund">Altes Stadthaus</a>, built in 1899 by Friedrich Kullrich</li>
<li>Romberg Park Gatehouse (17th century), once a gatehouse to a moated castle. Now it houses an art gallery.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Husen_Castle_(Syburg)" title="Husen Castle (Syburg)">Husen Castle</a>, the tower house of a former castle, in the borough of Syburg.</li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_buildings">Industrial buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Industrial buildings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The most industrial building in Dortmund are part of the <b>Industrial Heritage Trail</b> (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <span lang="de">Route der Industriekultur</span>). The trail links tourist attractions related to the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_heritage" title="Industrial heritage">industrial heritage</a> in the whole <a href="/wiki/Ruhr_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruhr area">Ruhr area</a> in <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> It is a part of the <a href="/wiki/European_Route_of_Industrial_Heritage" title="European Route of Industrial Heritage">European Route of Industrial Heritage</a>.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dortmund_U-Tower" title="Dortmund U-Tower">U-Tower</a>, former Dortmunder Union brewery, now a museum</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zollern_II/IV_Colliery" title="Zollern II/IV Colliery">Zollern II/IV Colliery</a>, now part of the Westphalian Industrial Museum and an Anchor Point of the <a href="/wiki/European_Route_of_Industrial_Heritage" title="European Route of Industrial Heritage">European Route of Industrial Heritage</a> (ERIH)</li>
<li>Hansa Coking Plant</li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_buildings">Cultural buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Cultural buildings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Konzerthaus Dortmund</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Opernhaus_Dortmund" title="Opernhaus Dortmund">Opernhaus Dortmund</a>, opera house built in 1966 on the site of the <a href="/wiki/Old_Synagogue_(Dortmund)" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Synagogue (Dortmund)">old synagogue</a> which was destroyed by the Nazis in 1938.</li>
<li>The major art museums include the <a href="/wiki/Museum_f%C3%BCr_Kunst_und_Kulturgeschichte" title="Museum für Kunst und Kulturgeschichte">Museum für Kunst und Kulturgeschichte</a> and the more recent <a href="/wiki/Museum_Ostwall" title="Museum Ostwall">Museum Ostwall</a>.</li>
<li>DASA, Germany Occupational Health and Safety Exhibition (German: Deutsche Arbeitsschutzausstellung)</li>
<li>Brewery Museum Dortmund</li>
<li>Museum of Art and Cultural History</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/German_Football_Museum" title="German Football Museum">German Football Museum</a></li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_important_buildings">Other important buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Other important buildings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Florianturm" title="Florianturm">Florianturm</a>, (television tower Florian)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Westfalenstadion" title="Westfalenstadion">Westfalenstadion</a>: Football ground of <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a>, licensed until 2021 under the name Signal Iduna Park <sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></li>
<li>Close to Westfalenstadion are the <a href="/wiki/Westfalenhallen" title="Westfalenhallen">Westfalenhallen</a>, a large convention centre, the site of several major conventions, trade fairs, ice-skating competitions, concerts and other major events since the 1950s.</li>
<li>Steinwache memorial</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="High-rise_structures">High-rise structures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: High-rise structures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dortmund tallest structure is the <a href="/wiki/Florianturm" title="Florianturm">Florianturm</a> telecommunication tower at 266&#160;m or 873&#160;ft. Other tall buildings are the churches around the city centre. A selection of the tallest office buildings in Dortmund is listed below.</p>
<ul>
<li>RWE Tower (100 metre-high skyscraper)</li>
<li>Westnetz Hochhaus Dortmund (100 metre-high skyscraper)</li>
<li>Westfalentower (88 metre-high skyscraper)</li>
<li>Harenberg City-Center (86 metre-high skyscraper)</li>
<li>Sparkassen-Hochhaus (70 metre-high skyscraper)</li>
<li>IWO-Hochhaus(70 metre-high skyscraper)</li>
<li>Ellipson (66 metre-high skyscraper)</li>
<li>Volkswohl Bund Hochhaus (60 metre-high skyscraper)</li>
</ul>
