<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road_transport">Road transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Road transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Schnettkerbruecke_West.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Schnettkerbruecke_West.jpg/220px-Schnettkerbruecke_West.jpg" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Schnettkerbruecke_West.jpg/330px-Schnettkerbruecke_West.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Schnettkerbruecke_West.jpg/440px-Schnettkerbruecke_West.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3426" data-file-height="2034" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Schnettkerbruecke_West.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_40" title="Bundesautobahn 40">Ruhrschnellweg</a> Section East Dortmund</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Dortmund also serves as a major European and German crossroads for the Autobahnsystem. The <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_40" title="Bundesautobahn 40">Ruhrschnellweg</a> follows old Hanseatic trade routes to connect the city with the other metropolises of the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruhr Area">Ruhr Area</a>. It crosses the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a>-German border as a continuation of the Dutch <a href="/wiki/A67_motorway_(Netherlands)" title="A67 motorway (Netherlands)">A67</a> and crosses the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a>, leads through the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr_valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruhr valley">Ruhr valley</a> toward <a href="/wiki/Bochum" title="Bochum">Bochum</a>, becoming B&#160;1 (<a href="/wiki/Bundesstra%C3%9Fe_1" title="Bundesstraße 1">Bundesstraße&#160;1</a>) at the Kreuz Dortmund West and eventually merging into the A&#160;44 near <a href="/wiki/Holzwickede" title="Holzwickede">Holzwickede</a>. It has officially been named Ruhrschnellweg (Ruhr Fast Way), but locals usually call it Ruhrschleichweg (Ruhr Crawling Way) or "the Ruhr area's longest parking lot". According to <i>Der Spiegel</i>, it is the most congested motorway in Germany.</p>
<p>Connections to more distant parts of Germany are maintained by Autobahn routes <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_1" title="Bundesautobahn 1">A1</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_2" title="Bundesautobahn 2">A2</a>, which traverse the north and east city limits and meet at the <a href="/wiki/Kamener_Kreuz" title="Kamener Kreuz">Kamener Kreuz</a> interchange north-east of Dortmund. In combination with the Autobahn <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_45" title="Bundesautobahn 45">A45</a> to the west these form the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund_Beltway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dortmund Beltway (page does not exist)">Dortmund Beltway</a> (<i>Dortmunder Autobahnring</i>).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail_transport">Rail transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Rail transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HBFDo.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/HBFDo.JPG/220px-HBFDo.JPG" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/HBFDo.JPG/330px-HBFDo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/HBFDo.JPG/440px-HBFDo.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1902" data-file-height="1438" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HBFDo.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dortmund central train station</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dortmund_M%C3%B6llerbr%C3%BCcke_HDR.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Dortmund_M%C3%B6llerbr%C3%BCcke_HDR.jpg/220px-Dortmund_M%C3%B6llerbr%C3%BCcke_HDR.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Dortmund_M%C3%B6llerbr%C3%BCcke_HDR.jpg/330px-Dortmund_M%C3%B6llerbr%C3%BCcke_HDR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Dortmund_M%C3%B6llerbr%C3%BCcke_HDR.jpg/440px-Dortmund_M%C3%B6llerbr%C3%BCcke_HDR.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dortmund_M%C3%B6llerbr%C3%BCcke_HDR.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Interchange station Möllerbrücke</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As with most communes in the Ruhr area, local transport is carried out by a local, publicly owned company for transport within the city, the <a href="/wiki/DB_Regio" title="DB Regio">DB Regio</a> subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a> for regional transport and Deutsche Bahn itself for long-distance journeys. The local carrier, Dortmunder Stadtwerke (DSW21), is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Verkehrsverbund_Rhein-Ruhr" title="Verkehrsverbund Rhein-Ruhr">Verkehrsverbund Rhein-Ruhr</a> (VRR) association of public transport companies in the Ruhr area, which provides a uniform fare structure in the whole region. Within the VRR region, tickets are valid on lines of all members as well as DB's <a href="/wiki/Railway_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Railway line">railway lines</a> (except the high-speed <a href="/wiki/InterCity" title="InterCity">InterCity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Intercity-Express" title="Intercity-Express">Intercity-Express</a> networks) and can be bought at ticket machines and service centres of DSW21, all other members of VRR, and DB.</p>
<p>The central train station (<a href="/wiki/Dortmund_Hauptbahnhof" title="Dortmund Hauptbahnhof">Dortmund Hauptbahnhof</a>) is the third largest long distance traffic junction in Germany. Dortmund has a railway service with <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a> <a href="/wiki/InterCity" title="InterCity">InterCity</a> and <a href="/wiki/InterCityExpress" class="mw-redirect" title="InterCityExpress">ICE</a>-trains stopping at <i><a href="/wiki/Dortmund_Hauptbahnhof" title="Dortmund Hauptbahnhof">Dortmund Hauptbahnhof</a></i> (Dortmund Main Station). ICE and <a href="/wiki/Thalys" title="Thalys">TGV Thalys</a> high-speed trains link Dortmund with <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, Brussels (in 2h 30) and Paris (in 3h 50). There are frequent ICE trains to other German cities, including <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_am_Main" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt am Main">Frankfurt am Main</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> and other cities in the Rhein-Ruhr Region.</p>
<p>For public transportation, the city has an extensive <a href="/wiki/Dortmund_Stadtbahn" title="Dortmund Stadtbahn">Stadtbahn</a> and bus system. The U-Bahn has eight lines (U41 to U49) serving Dortmund and the large suburb of <a href="/wiki/L%C3%BCnen" title="Lünen">Lünen</a> in the north. The trains that run on the line are in fact lightrails as many lines travel along a track in the middle of the street instead of underground further from the city centre. The minimum service interval is 2.5 minutes, although the usual pattern is that each line runs at 5 to 10 minute intervals. In April 2008, the newly constructed east-west underground light rail line was opened, completing the underground service in the city centre and replacing the last <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">trams</a> on the surface.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>A number of bus lines complete the Dortmund public transport system. Night buses replace U-Bahn and tram services between 1:30 am and 3:30 am. The central junction for the night bus service is Reinoldikirche in the city centre, where all night bus lines start and end.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/H-Bahn" title="H-Bahn">H-Bahn</a> at <a href="/wiki/Dortmund_University_of_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Dortmund University of Technology">Dortmund University of Technology</a> is a hanging monorail built specifically to shuttle passengers between the university's two campuses,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> which are now also flanked by research laboratories and other high-tech corporations and startups. A nearly identical monorail system transfers passengers at <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Airport" title="Düsseldorf Airport">Düsseldorf Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_transport">Air transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Air transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Dortmund_Airport" title="Dortmund Airport">Dortmund Airport</a> is a medium-sized, but fast growing airport 13&#160;km (8.1&#160;mi) east of the city centre at the city limit to <a href="/wiki/Holzwickede" title="Holzwickede">Holzwickede</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The closest intercontinental airport is <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Airport" title="Düsseldorf Airport">Düsseldorf Airport</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_transport">Water transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Water transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Dortmund_Harbour" class="mw-redirect" title="Dortmund Harbour">Dortmund Harbour</a> (<i>Hafen</i>) is the largest canal harbour in Europe and the 11th fluvial harbour in Germany.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dortmund-0030-City-RWE.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Dortmund-0030-City-RWE.jpg/220px-Dortmund-0030-City-RWE.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Dortmund-0030-City-RWE.jpg/330px-Dortmund-0030-City-RWE.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Dortmund-0030-City-RWE.jpg/440px-Dortmund-0030-City-RWE.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2762" data-file-height="2054" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dortmund-0030-City-RWE.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Central business district "Wallring"</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Dortmund has adapted since the collapse of its century long steel, coal and beer industries. The region has shifted to high technology, <a href="/wiki/Robotics" title="Robotics">robotics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biomedical_technology" title="Biomedical technology">biomedical technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Micro_systems_technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Micro systems technology">micro systems technology</a>, engineering, tourism, finance, education and also <a href="/wiki/Service_(economics)" title="Service (economics)">services</a>. In 2009, Dortmund was classified as a <i>Node city</i> in the <i>Innovation Cities Index</i> published by 2thinknow.<sup id="cite_ref-innovation-cities.com_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-innovation-cities.com-4">[4]</a></sup> Hundreds of <a href="/wiki/Small_and_medium_enterprises" class="mw-redirect" title="Small and medium enterprises">SMEs</a> are still based in and around Dortmund (often termed <i><a href="/wiki/Mittelstand" title="Mittelstand">Mittelstand</a></i>). Dortmund is also home to a number of medium-sized information technology companies,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> many linked to the local university <a href="/wiki/TU_Dortmund" class="mw-redirect" title="TU Dortmund">TU Dortmund</a> at the first technology center in <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> named "Technologiepark Dortmund" opened in the 1980s. With around 280 companies like <a href="/wiki/Boehringer_Ingelheim" title="Boehringer Ingelheim">Boehringer Ingelheim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Communications" title="Verizon Communications">Verizon Communications</a> and more than 8,500 employees, TechnologiePark Dortmund is one of the most successful technology parks in Europe. The city works closely with research institutes, private universities, and companies to collaborate on the commercialisation of science initiatives.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> In the last years a service sector and high-tech industry grow up. Some of its most prominent companies of these sector include <a href="/wiki/Wilo_SE" class="mw-redirect" title="Wilo SE">Wilo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amprion" title="Amprion">Amprion</a>, <a href="/wiki/RWE" title="RWE">RWE-Westnetz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhenus_(company)" title="Rhenus (company)">Rhenus Logistics</a>, <a href="/wiki/KHS_GmbH" title="KHS GmbH">KHS GmbH</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elmos_Semiconductor" title="Elmos Semiconductor">Elmos Semiconductor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Signal_Iduna" title="Signal Iduna">Signal Iduna</a> and <a href="/wiki/ABP_Induction_Systems" title="ABP Induction Systems">ABP Induction Systems</a> – all of whom have their headquarters here. Companies with operations in or around Dortmund include <a href="/wiki/Zalando" title="Zalando">Zalando</a>, <a href="/wiki/Daimler_AG" title="Daimler AG">Daimler AG</a>: EvoBus, <a href="/wiki/RapidMiner" title="RapidMiner">RapidMiner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gap_Inc." title="Gap Inc.">Gap Inc.</a> and <a href="/wiki/ThyssenKrupp" title="ThyssenKrupp">ThyssenKrupp</a></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Logistic">Logistic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Logistic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dortmund is one of the most important <a href="/wiki/Logistics" title="Logistics">logistic</a> hubs in Germany, more than 900 companies working in logistics, as well as nationally and internationally recognised scientific institutes. The variety of different activities taking place at the Fraunhofer Institute Material Flow and Logistics (<a href="/wiki/Fraunhofer_Society" title="Fraunhofer Society">Fraunhofer Society</a>) has, over the past few years, led to a bundling of skills in the areas of logistics and digitalisation in the city. Industry-based initiatives and pilot projects, such as the Hybrid Services in Logistics innovation lab, the efficiency cluster LogistikRuhr, Industrial Data Space, the Dortmund Mittelstand 4.0 Centre of Excellence, and the enterprise labs. The Digital Hub for Logistics of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Ministry_for_Economic_Affairs_and_Energy" title="Federal Ministry for Economic Affairs and Energy">Federal Ministry for Economic Affairs and Energy</a> is based in Dortmund and twinned with <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>.</p>
<p>Companies with big logistic hubs for Germany and Europe in Dortmund include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon.com">Amazon</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/IKEA" title="IKEA">IKEA</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Decathlon" title="Decathlon">Decathlon</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rhenus_(company)" title="Rhenus (company)">Rhenus Logistics</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Schenker_AG" title="Schenker AG">Schenker AG</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fairs">Fairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Fairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dortmund is home to Germany's twelve biggest exhibition centre, <a href="/wiki/Westfalenhallen" title="Westfalenhallen">Halls of Westphalia</a> which lies near the city center next to <a href="/wiki/Dortmund_Airport" title="Dortmund Airport">Dortmund Airport</a>. With around 77.000 visitors each year, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagd_%26_Hund&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jagd &amp; Hund (page does not exist)">Jagd &amp; Hund</a> is by far the largest event held there. Other important fairs open to consumers include "Intermodelbau", the world's biggest consumer fair for model making, and one of the leading fairs for youth culture "YOU". Important fairs restricted to professionals include "D.I.M" (Deutsche Immobilienmesse, German property fair), Creativa (Hobby) and InterTabac (Tabaco).<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Consulates">Consulates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Consulates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>As a profoundly international city, Dortmund hosts diplomatic missions (<a href="/wiki/Consulate" class="mw-redirect" title="Consulate">consulates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Consulate-_general" class="mw-redirect" title="Consulate- general">consulates-general</a>) of <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup>,the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup>, and <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Courts">Courts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Courts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Several <a href="/wiki/Court" title="Court">courts</a> are located in Dortmund, including:</p>
<ul>
<li><b>Landgericht Dortmund</b> (Regional Court Dortmund)</li>
<li><b>Amtsgericht Dortmund</b> (Local Court Dortmund)</li>
<li><b>Sozialgericht Dortmund</b> (Social Court Dortmund)</li>
<li><b>Arbeitsgericht Dortmund</b> (Employment Court Dortmund)</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Newspapers">Newspapers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Newspapers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Two important daily newspapers are published in and around Dortmund. The conservative <i><a href="/wiki/Ruhr_Nachrichten" title="Ruhr Nachrichten">Ruhr Nachrichten</a></i>, also known as <i>RN</i>, was founded in 1949. The RN has a circulation of over 225,000 copies daily. The other important newspaper, the <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Westf%C3%A4lische_Rundschau&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Westfälische Rundschau (page does not exist)">Westfälische Rundschau</a></i>, was first published in 1945 and has a daily circulation of over 181,000. The WR is published by Germany's third largest newspaper and magazine publisher <i><a href="/wiki/Funke_Mediengruppe" title="Funke Mediengruppe">Funke Mediengruppe</a>'.'</i></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Magazines">Magazines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Magazines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Several magazines also originate from Dortmund. The Rock <i><a href="/wiki/Rock_hard_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rock hard (magazine)">Rock hard (magazine)</a></i> is a <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">metal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hard_rock" title="Hard rock">hard rock</a> magazine, with subsidiaries in various countries worldwide, including <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>/<a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>.<i>Visions</i> is a German music magazine with a circulation of approximately 35,000.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio_and_TV">Radio and TV</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Radio and TV">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Westdeutscher_Rundfunk" title="Westdeutscher Rundfunk">Westdeutscher Rundfunk</a> (WDR, West German Broadcasting Cologne has a big studio in Dortmund, which is responsible for the east <a href="/wiki/Ruhr" title="Ruhr">Ruhr</a> area. Each day, it produces a 30-minute regional evening news magazine (called <i>Lokalzeit Ruhr</i>), a 5-minute afternoon news programme, and several radio news programmes. A local broadcasting station called Radio 91.2 went "on-the-air" in the early 1990s. <a href="/wiki/Sat.1" title="Sat.1">Sat.1</a> have a regional studio in Dortmund</p>
<p>Two big Radio Channels of <a href="/wiki/Westdeutscher_Rundfunk" title="Westdeutscher Rundfunk">Westdeutscher Rundfunk</a> are sending from Dortmund.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/WDR_2" title="WDR 2">WDR 2</a>, featuring adult-oriented popular music, focuses strongly on national and regional news, current affairs, and sport.</li>
<li>WDR 4 (motto: <i>Melodien für ein gutes Gefühl</i>, "Melodies for a good feeling") is a channel aimed chiefly towards an older audience. Its focus is on tuneful music – in particular, <a href="/wiki/Oldies" title="Oldies">oldies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Classic_hits" title="Classic hits">classic hits</a>: popular music of the 1960s to the 1980s or later – with more specialized programming (operetta, country, folk) in the evenings. Around 30-40% of WDR 4's musical output is made up of <a href="/wiki/German-language" class="mw-redirect" title="German-language">German-language</a> songs.</li>
</ul>
<p>Other radio broadcasters include Radio NRW and eldoradio*.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Technical_University_of_Dortmund" title="Technical University of Dortmund">Technical University of Dortmund</a> founded in 1968 is located in the southern part of the city. It has about 30,000 students and a wide range of subjects in of <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electrical_engineering" title="Electrical engineering">electrical engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">chemistry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spatial_planning" title="Spatial planning">spatial planning</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economics" title="Economics">economics</a>. The university has its own train station at the campus’s main gate which is only seven minutes away from the city center. The university’s most noticeable landmark is the <a href="/wiki/H-Bahn" title="H-Bahn">H-Bahn</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Monorail" title="Monorail">monorail</a> train which connects the north and south campuses.</p>
<p>The city is the site of several other universities, colleges and academies, which attract about 45,000 students.<sup id="cite_ref-dev.statistik.dortmund.de_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dev.statistik.dortmund.de-19">[19]</a></sup> Among them there are:</p>
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Fachhochschule_Dortmund" class="mw-redirect" title="Fachhochschule Dortmund">Fachhochschule Dortmund</a></i>: University of Applied Sciences founded in 1971.</li>
<li><i>FOM Hochschule für Oekonomie &amp; Management, Standort Dortmund</i>: Academy for management, founded in 1993.</li>
<li><i>Fachhochschule für öffentliche Verwaltung Nordrhein-Westfalen</i>: Academy for public administration.</li>
<li><i>International School of Management</i>: Private academy focussing on management and economics, founded in 1990.</li>
<li><i>IT-Center Dortmund</i>: Private college founded in 2000.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dortmunder-U-2011_0684.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Dortmunder-U-2011_0684.jpg/220px-Dortmunder-U-2011_0684.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Dortmunder-U-2011_0684.jpg/330px-Dortmunder-U-2011_0684.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Dortmunder-U-2011_0684.jpg/440px-Dortmunder-U-2011_0684.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4401" data-file-height="3239" /></a>

<a href="/wiki/Dortmund_U-Tower" title="Dortmund U-Tower">Dortmund U-Tower</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mayday_2009_dortmund_halle_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Mayday_2009_dortmund_halle_1.jpg/220px-Mayday_2009_dortmund_halle_1.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Mayday_2009_dortmund_halle_1.jpg/330px-Mayday_2009_dortmund_halle_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Mayday_2009_dortmund_halle_1.jpg/440px-Mayday_2009_dortmund_halle_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4009" data-file-height="2673" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mayday_2009_dortmund_halle_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mayday 2009 Westfalenhallen</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city has a long tradition of music and theatre. The orchestra was founded in 1887 and is now called <a href="/wiki/Dortmunder_Philharmoniker" title="Dortmunder Philharmoniker">Dortmunder Philharmoniker</a>. The first opera house was built in 1904, destroyed in World War II and opened again in 1966 as <a href="/wiki/Opernhaus_Dortmund" title="Opernhaus Dortmund">Opernhaus Dortmund</a>. It is operated by <a href="/wiki/Theater_Dortmund" title="Theater Dortmund">Theater Dortmund</a> together with other locations, including (since 2002) the Konzerthaus Dortmund. The Konzerthaus Dortmund is listed in the ECHO list as one of the 21 most outstanding concert halls in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Dortmund U-Tower, which was once a brewery, is now European centre for creative economy and the <a href="/wiki/Museum_am_Ostwall" class="mw-redirect" title="Museum am Ostwall">Museum am Ostwall</a>. The area around the U-Tower called "Union Viertel" is part of the Creative.Quarters Ruhr and are rooted in the European Capital of Culture <a href="/wiki/RUHR.2010" class="mw-redirect" title="RUHR.2010">RUHR.2010</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals_and_Nightlife">Festivals and Nightlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Festivals and Nightlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dortmund offers a variety of restaurants, bars and clubs. Clubs concentrate in and around the city centre (Wallring) and in the Kreuzviertel district. After the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Molotov_(club)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Molotov (club) (page does not exist)">Molotov</a> in Hamburg and the <a href="/wiki/Berghain" title="Berghain">Berghain</a> in Berlin, the FZW (Freizeitzentrum West) in the Union district is one of the three best clubs in Germany. With 307 events in 2015, including concerts, parties, festivals, readings and football public viewings have strengthened the FZW's reputation as an "it club" in the Ruhr region.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Furthermore, Dortmund is one of the main centres of the Electronic dance music and techno subculture. With the <a href="/wiki/Mayday_(music_festival)" title="Mayday (music festival)">Mayday</a> and Syndicate festivals, the Westfalenhalle Arena has become one of the most important techno strongholds in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>. After negotiations with several German cities, it was announced that the <a href="/wiki/Love_Parade" title="Love Parade">Love Parade</a> would move to the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruhr Area">Ruhr Area</a> for five years (2007-2012). After <a href="/wiki/Essen" title="Essen">Essen</a> in 2007 the festival took 2008 place on the <a href="/wiki/Bundesstra%C3%9Fe_1" title="Bundesstraße 1">Bundesstraße 1</a> under the motto <i>Highway of Love</i>. The event was planned as a "Love Weekend", with parties throughout the region. For the first time the Turkish electronic scene was represented by its own float, called "<a href="/wiki/Turkish_Delights_(music_project)" title="Turkish Delights (music project)">Turkish Delights</a>". The official estimate is that 1.6 million visitors attended, making it the largest parade to date.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>Every year, the Juicy Beats music festival turns the Westfalenpark into a huge festival ground for pop, rap, electro, indie, alternative, reggae and urban beats - most recently with over 50,000 visitors.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Traditional meals in the region are <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfefferpotthast&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pfefferpotthast (page does not exist)">Pfefferpotthast</a> (kind of Goulash with a lot of beef), <a href="/wiki/Himmel_und_erde" class="mw-redirect" title="Himmel und erde">Heaven and Earth</a> (Himmel und Äd; <a href="/wiki/Black_pudding" title="Black pudding">black pudding</a> with stewed apples mixed with <a href="/wiki/Mashed_potato" title="Mashed potato">mashed potatoes</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Pumpernickel" title="Pumpernickel">Pumpernickel</a> with Griebenschmalz (German lard with crispy pieces of pork skin)</p>
<p>In summer the people like to eat a Dortmunder Salzkuchen (Bread buns with caraway fruits, salt, meat and onions). Also a special meal in the winter is <a href="/wiki/Reibekuchen" title="Reibekuchen">Reibekuchen</a> (fried potato pancake served with apple sauce).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gesch%C3%A4ftsstelle_BVB_Rheinlanddamm.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Gesch%C3%A4ftsstelle_BVB_Rheinlanddamm.jpg/220px-Gesch%C3%A4ftsstelle_BVB_Rheinlanddamm.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Gesch%C3%A4ftsstelle_BVB_Rheinlanddamm.jpg/330px-Gesch%C3%A4ftsstelle_BVB_Rheinlanddamm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Gesch%C3%A4ftsstelle_BVB_Rheinlanddamm.jpg/440px-Gesch%C3%A4ftsstelle_BVB_Rheinlanddamm.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264" /></a>

</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Handball-Bundesliga_GmbH_Hauptverwaltung.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Handball-Bundesliga_GmbH_Hauptverwaltung.jpg/220px-Handball-Bundesliga_GmbH_Hauptverwaltung.jpg" width="220" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Handball-Bundesliga_GmbH_Hauptverwaltung.jpg/330px-Handball-Bundesliga_GmbH_Hauptverwaltung.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Handball-Bundesliga_GmbH_Hauptverwaltung.jpg/440px-Handball-Bundesliga_GmbH_Hauptverwaltung.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3189" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

Headquarter DHB</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Dortmund calls itself <i>Sportstadt</i> (City of Sports). The city is the home of the biggest Handball Association in the world the <a href="/wiki/German_Handball_Association" title="German Handball Association">German Handball Association</a> (German: Deutscher Handballbund) (DHB) and the German professional handball league <a href="/wiki/Handball-Bundesliga" title="Handball-Bundesliga">Handball-Bundesliga</a> (HBL). Furthermore, Dortmund is home of the Olympic centre of Westphalia.</p>
<p>The city is home of many sports clubs, iconic athletes and annually organises several world-renowned sporting events. Some examples are the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ruhrmarathon&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ruhrmarathon (page does not exist)">Ruhrmarathon</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dortmund_Sparkassen_Chess_Meeting" title="Dortmund Sparkassen Chess Meeting">Sparkassen Chess-Meeting</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dortmund_Signal_Iduna_Park_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Dortmund_Signal_Iduna_Park_1.jpg/220px-Dortmund_Signal_Iduna_Park_1.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Dortmund_Signal_Iduna_Park_1.jpg/330px-Dortmund_Signal_Iduna_Park_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Dortmund_Signal_Iduna_Park_1.jpg/440px-Dortmund_Signal_Iduna_Park_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="852" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dortmund_Signal_Iduna_Park_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Signal_Iduna_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Signal Iduna Park">Signal Iduna Park</a>, the home stadium of <a href="/wiki/Fu%C3%9Fball-Bundesliga" class="mw-redirect" title="Fußball-Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> club <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a>, is the biggest stadium in Germany</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Dortmund is home to the sports club <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a>, one of the most successful clubs in German <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> history. Borussia Dortmund are former <a href="/wiki/Fu%C3%9Fball-Bundesliga" class="mw-redirect" title="Fußball-Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> champions most recently in 2011–2012. Borussia Dortmund was winner of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Intercontinental_Cup_(football)" title="Intercontinental Cup (football)">Intercontinental Cup</a> in 1997, as well as the UEFA Cup Winners' Cup in 1966. This made it the first European Cup Winner in Germany. 'Die Borussen' are eight-time German Champions and have won three German Cups. Borussia Dortmund play at <a href="/wiki/Westfalenstadion" title="Westfalenstadion">Westfalenstadion</a>, currently known as Signal Iduna Park. It was built for the <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1974 FIFA World Cup">1974 FIFA World Cup</a> and also hosted some matches of <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 FIFA World Cup</a>. It is Germany's largest football stadium with a maximum capacity of 81,359 spectators.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stadion_%22Rote_Erde%22_in_Dortmund_-_panoramio_(4).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Stadion_%22Rote_Erde%22_in_Dortmund_-_panoramio_%284%29.jpg/220px-Stadion_%22Rote_Erde%22_in_Dortmund_-_panoramio_%284%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Stadion_%22Rote_Erde%22_in_Dortmund_-_panoramio_%284%29.jpg/330px-Stadion_%22Rote_Erde%22_in_Dortmund_-_panoramio_%284%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Stadion_%22Rote_Erde%22_in_Dortmund_-_panoramio_%284%29.jpg/440px-Stadion_%22Rote_Erde%22_in_Dortmund_-_panoramio_%284%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Handball">Handball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Handball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Borussia Dortmund also has a women's handball team playing in the first <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga_(handball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bundesliga (handball)">Bundesliga</a></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Table_Tennis">Table Tennis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Table Tennis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Borussia Dortmund also <a href="/wiki/Table_tennis" title="Table tennis">table tennis</a> team playing in the first Bundesliga.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="American_Football">American Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: American Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Dortmund_Giants" title="Dortmund Giants">Dortmund Giants</a> established on 22 May 1980 are an American football team from Dortmund. The official name of the club is 1. Dortmunder Footballclub Dortmund 1980 "Giants" e.V..The club spent the 1994 season in the 2. Bundesliga before dropping for two seasons to the tier three <a href="/wiki/American_football_Regionalliga" title="American football Regionalliga">Regionalliga West</a>. Five more 2. Bundesliga seasons followed from 1997 to 2001, the final one in a combined team with the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bochum_Cadets&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bochum Cadets (page does not exist)">Bochum Cadets</a> as the Dortmund B1 Giants.<sup id="cite_ref-Fhist_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fhist-53">[53]</a></sup> After a five-season spell in the Regionalliga the club finished the 2014 season without a win and had to return to the Oberliga once more.<sup id="cite_ref-Fhist_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fhist-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EHC_Dortmund,_indoor.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/EHC_Dortmund%2C_indoor.jpg/220px-EHC_Dortmund%2C_indoor.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/EHC_Dortmund%2C_indoor.jpg/330px-EHC_Dortmund%2C_indoor.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/EHC_Dortmund%2C_indoor.jpg/440px-EHC_Dortmund%2C_indoor.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EHC_Dortmund,_indoor.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Eissportzentrum Westfalenhallen</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ice_Hockey">Ice Hockey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Ice Hockey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/EHC_Dortmund" title="EHC Dortmund">Eisadler Dortmund</a> is the city's ice hockey club who play in <a href="/wiki/Eissportzentrum_Westfalenhallen" title="Eissportzentrum Westfalenhallen">Eissportzentrum Westfalenhallen</a> a <a href="/wiki/Arena" title="Arena">indoor sporting arena</a> at the Strobelallee. They play 2016/17 in the Oberliga, the third level of ice hockey in Germany.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Basketball">Basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Basketball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city's Basketball club is SVD 49 Dortmund basketball team play in their respective second national divisions.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Baseball">Baseball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Baseball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city's Baseball club is Dortmund Wanderers play in the first <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga_(baseball)" title="Bundesliga (baseball)">Bundesliga</a></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_Sports">Other Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Other Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Dortmund_Sparkassen_Chess_Meeting" title="Dortmund Sparkassen Chess Meeting">Sparkassen Chess-Meeting</a> has been hosted in Dortmund since 1982.</p>
<p>Besides Dortmund owns an all-weather racecourse called "Galopprennbahn Dortmund".</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Born_before_1900">Born before 1900</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Born before 1900">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1979-013-43,_Wilhelm_Canaris.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1979-013-43%2C_Wilhelm_Canaris.jpg/150px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1979-013-43%2C_Wilhelm_Canaris.jpg" width="150" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1979-013-43%2C_Wilhelm_Canaris.jpg/225px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1979-013-43%2C_Wilhelm_Canaris.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1979-013-43%2C_Wilhelm_Canaris.jpg/300px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1979-013-43%2C_Wilhelm_Canaris.jpg 2x" data-file-width="540" data-file-height="797" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1979-013-43,_Wilhelm_Canaris.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Wilhelm Canaris 1940</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Arnold_Brockhaus" title="Friedrich Arnold Brockhaus">Friedrich Arnold Brockhaus</a> (1772-1823), publisher, founder of the publishing house "F. A. Brockhaus "and editor of <a href="/wiki/Brockhaus_Encyclopedia" class="mw-redirect" title="Brockhaus Encyclopedia">Brockhaus</a></li>
<li>William Middendorf (1793-1853), theologian and educator</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Emil_Anneke" title="Emil Anneke">Emil Anneke</a> (1823-1888), revolutionary and American journalist and lawyer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_L%C3%BCbke" title="Wilhelm Lübke">Wilhelm Lübke</a> (1826-1893), art historian</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Adolf_Schmal" title="Adolf Schmal">Adolf Schmal</a> (1872-1919), Austrian sports man</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Canaris" title="Wilhelm Canaris">Wilhelm Canaris</a> (1887-1945), admiral and chief of the military intelligence service</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Walter_Blume_(SS_officer)" title="Walter Blume (SS officer)">Walter Blume</a> (1906-1974), lawyer and SS officer</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Born_1901-1950">Born 1901-1950</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Born 1901-1950">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Walter_Haenisch" title="Walter Haenisch">Walter Haenisch</a> (1905-1938), author, communist, victim of Stalinism</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fritz_Henle" title="Fritz Henle">Fritz Henle</a> (1909-1993), photographer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Albrecht_Brandi" title="Albrecht Brandi">Albrecht Brandi</a> (1914-1966), naval officer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Heinz_Stahlschmidt" class="mw-redirect" title="Heinz Stahlschmidt">Heinz Stahlschmidt</a> (1919-2010), sergeant and fire fighter</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dieter_Wellershoff" title="Dieter Wellershoff">Dieter Wellershoff</a> (1933-2005), admiral, <a href="/wiki/Inspector_General_of_the_Bundeswehr" title="Inspector General of the Bundeswehr">Inspector General of the Bundeswehr</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Cyliax" title="Gerhard Cyliax">Gerhard Cyliax</a> (1934-2008), football player</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Elga_Andersen" title="Elga Andersen">Elga Andersen</a> (1935-1994), actress and singer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hans_Tilkowski" title="Hans Tilkowski">Hans Tilkowski</a> (born 1935), football goalkeeper and coach</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dieter_Fenske" title="Dieter Fenske">Dieter Fenske</a> (born 1942), inorganic chemist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Christine_Haidegger" title="Christine Haidegger">Christine Haidegger</a> (born 1942), Austrian writer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Annegret_Richter" title="Annegret Richter">Annegret Richter</a> (born 1950), sprinter</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hermann_Spieckermann" title="Hermann Spieckermann">Hermann Spieckermann</a> (born 1950), Protestant theologian</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Born_after_1950">Born after 1950</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmund&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Born after 1950">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Klaus_Niedzwiedz" title="Klaus Niedzwiedz">Klaus Niedzwiedz</a> (born 1951), racing driver and television presenter</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ulla_Burchardt" title="Ulla Burchardt">Ulla Burchardt</a> (born 1954), politician (SPD)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Klaus_Segbers" title="Klaus Segbers">Klaus Segbers</a> (born 1954), a political scientist and professor</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Achim_Peters" title="Achim Peters">Achim Peters</a> (born 1957), obesity specialist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dietmar_B%C3%A4r" title="Dietmar Bär">Dietmar Bär</a> (born 1961), actor</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stefan_Heinig" title="Stefan Heinig">Stefan Heinig</a> (born 1962), director and shareholder</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Martin_Zawieja" title="Martin Zawieja">Martin Zawieja</a> (born 1963), weightlifter</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ralf_Husmann" title="Ralf Husmann">Ralf Husmann</a> (born 1964), writer, producer and author</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vincent_Mennie" class="mw-redirect" title="Vincent Mennie">Vincent Mennie</a> (born 1964), Scottish footballer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Matthias_Kohring" title="Matthias Kohring">Matthias Kohring</a> (born 1965), media and communications scientist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Erkau" title="André Erkau">André Erkau</a> (born 1968), director and screenwriter</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Yasemin_%C5%9Eamdereli" title="Yasemin Şamdereli">Yasemin Şamdereli</a> (born 1973), film director and screenwriter</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kevin_Grosskreutz" class="mw-redirect" title="Kevin Grosskreutz">Kevin Grosskreutz</a> (born 1988), football player</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Marco_Reus" title="Marco Reus">Marco Reus</a> (born 1989), football player</li>
</ul>

<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="3" style="padding:0.2em 0.4em 0.4em;line-height:1.25em;">
<div>
<div class="plainlist">
<ul>
<li><sup><small>1</small></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> and <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Dortmund</a> were both capital of the Westphalian Quarter at different times.</li>
<li><sup><small>2</small></sup> <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> gained importance once <a href="/wiki/Bruges" title="Bruges">Bruges</a> became inaccessible due to the silting of the <a href="/wiki/Zwin" title="Zwin">Zwin</a> channel.</li>
</ul>
</div>

</th>
